   - **Option [1]**: Move robber to (0, -1, 1) and steal from RED. This blocks RED's sheep tile production.
   - **Option [2]**: Move robber to (-1, 0, 1) and steal from RED. This blocks RED's wheat tile production.
   - **Option [3]**: Move robber to (-1, 1, 0) and steal from RED. This blocks RED's wheat tile production.
   - **Option [7]**: Move robber to (1, -2, 1) and steal from RED. This blocks RED's ore tile production.
   - **Option [9]**: Move robber to (-1, -1, 2) and steal from RED. This blocks RED's ore tile production.
   - **Option [10]**: Move robber to (-2, 0, 2) and steal from RED. This blocks RED's wood tile production.
   - **Option [11]**: Move robber to (-2, 1, 1) and steal from RED. This blocks RED's wood tile production.

5. **Best Option**:
   - Moving the robber to a tile that blocks a critical resource for RED and allows stealing a resource from RED is ideal.
   - Given RED's resource distribution, blocking the ore tile (option [7]) or the wheat tile (option [2] or [3]) would be most impactful.
   - Since ore is generally harder to obtain and is crucial for city upgrades, blocking the ore tile (option [7]) and stealing a resource from RED is the best move.

### Final Decision:
\[ \boxed{7} \]

   - Buying a development card could provide a knight to move the robber or a victory point card, but it doesn't directly help us acquire the needed WOOD.

6. **Strategic Decision**:
   - Since we cannot acquire WOOD immediately and buying a development card does not directly help with our current plan, the best option is to end the turn and hope for better resource acquisition in the next turn.

<plan>Continue with the plan to build a settlement at node 36. Focus on acquiring 🌲WOOD to complete the settlement. Then, upgrade settlements to cities and expand the road network.</plan>
